    function loadScript(url, callback) {
      var script = document.createElement("script");
      script.type = "text/javascript";
    
      if (script.readyState) {  //Internet Explorer
          script.onreadystatechange = function() {
            if (script.readyState == "loaded" ||
                    script.readyState == "complete") {
              script.onreadystatechange = null;
              callback();
            }
          };
      } else {  //Other browsers
        script.onload = function() {
          callback();
        };
      }
    
      script.src = url;
      document.getElementsByTagName("head")[0].appendChild(script);
    }

      AppleID.auth.init({

<div id="descriptionContainer">
  
      <div id="description" class="readable stacked" style="right:0">
        
<span id="freeTextContainer17623142282963218048">Kehadiran roman sejarah ini, bukan saja dimaksudkan untuk mengisi sebuah episode berbangsa yang berada di titik persalinan yang pelik dan menentukan, namun juga mengisi isu kesusastraan yang sangat minim menggarap periode pelik ini. Karena itu hadirnya roman ini memberi bacaan alternatif kepada kita untuk melihat jalan dan gelombang sejarah secara lain dan dari sisinya yan</span>
  <span id="freeText17623142282963218048" style="display:none">Kehadiran roman sejarah ini, bukan saja dimaksudkan untuk mengisi sebuah episode berbangsa yang berada di titik persalinan yang pelik dan menentukan, namun juga mengisi isu kesusastraan yang sangat minim menggarap periode pelik ini. Karena itu hadirnya roman ini memberi bacaan alternatif kepada kita untuk melihat jalan dan gelombang sejarah secara lain dan dari sisinya yang berbeda.<br /><br />Tetralogi ini dibagi dalam format empat buku. Pembagian ini bisa juga kita artikan sebagai pembelahan pergerakan yang hadir dalam beberapa periode. Dan roman ketiga ini, <i>Jejak Langkah</i>, adalah fase pengorganisasian perlawanan.<br /><br />Minke memobilisasi segala daya untuk melawan bercokolnya kekuasaan Hindia yang sudah berabad-abad umurnya. Namun Minke tak pilih perlawanan bersenjata. Ia memilih jalan jurnalistik dengan membuat sebanyak-banyaknya bacaan Pribumi. Yang paling terkenal tentu saja Medan Prijaji.<br /><br />Dengan koran ini, Minke berseru-seru kepada rakyat Pribumi tiga hal: meningkatkan boikot, berorganisasi, dan menghapuskan kebudayaan feodalistik. Sekaligus lewat langkah jurnalistik, Minke berseru-seru: "Didiklah rakyat dengan organisasi dan didiklah penguasa dengan perlawanan".</span>
  <a data-text-id="17623142282963218048" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

      </div>
</div>

    <div class="section firstReview">
      

<div id="review_37334147" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/37334147" />
    <a title="Brian" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/1551688-brian"><img alt="Brian" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1241751092p2/1551688.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/37334147?book_show_action=true">Nov 10, 2008</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Brian" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Brian" href="/user/show/1551688-brian">Brian</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="ebook 9781101615348" href="/book/show/333078.Footsteps">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1551688-brian?shelf=asian">asian</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1551688-brian?shelf=read-2009">read-2009</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer37334147" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer17033393867645992412">The first book in this quartet <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/6060001.This_Earth_of_Mankind__The_Buru_Quartet_' title='This Earth of Mankind (The Buru Quartet) by Pramoedya Ananta Toer' rel='nofollow noopener'>This Earth of Mankind</a> made me cry. The second book <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/248069.Child_of_All_Nations__Buru_Quartet_' title='Child of All Nations (Buru Quartet) by Pramoedya Ananta Toer' rel='nofollow noopener'>Child of All Nations</a> made me cry. This third installment of the Buru Quartet made me angry. Colonization just sucks. And when a nation of mixed cultures fight each other while working towards independence, freedom if achieved is tainted. Footsteps is the biggest of the quartet and the most political. From what I understand it is also the last of the first person narrative from Minke's point of view. One more to go </span>
  <span id="freeText17033393867645992412" style="display:none">The first book in this quartet <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/6060001.This_Earth_of_Mankind__The_Buru_Quartet_" title="This Earth of Mankind (The Buru Quartet) by Pramoedya Ananta Toer" rel="nofollow noopener">This Earth of Mankind</a> made me cry. The second book <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/248069.Child_of_All_Nations__Buru_Quartet_" title="Child of All Nations (Buru Quartet) by Pramoedya Ananta Toer" rel="nofollow noopener">Child of All Nations</a> made me cry. This third installment of the Buru Quartet made me angry. Colonization just sucks. And when a nation of mixed cultures fight each other while working towards independence, freedom if achieved is tainted. Footsteps is the biggest of the quartet and the most political. From what I understand it is also the last of the first person narrative from Minke's point of view. One more to go and I really hope that Indonesia gets it together... but now in 2009 I know how <i>this earth of mankind</i> stands both politically and culturally and I don't know if Minke would be proud.<br /><br /><i>"So what is the use of the French Revolution then?" and her voice was so gentle, as it had always been ever since the first time I heard it. "You said it was to free men from the burdens made by other men. Wasn't that it? That is not Javanese. A Javanese does something with no other motive than to do it. Orders come from Allah, from the gods, from the Raja. After a Javanese has carried out the order, he will feel satisfied because he has become himself. And then he waits for the next order. So the Javanese are grateful, they give thanks. They are not preyed upon by monsters within themselves."</i><br /><br />Although nominated for the Nobel Prize in Literature, Pramoedya Ananta Toer gave up his chance of ever winning when he died. Damn it, why didn't he wait a little longer before dying?</span>
  <a data-text-id="17033393867645992412" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2651816975" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer17569860625311644622">This is the third book of the Buru Quartet I've read and the 4th novel I've read from the greatest Indonesian author of all time, Pramoedya Ananta Toer. I've loved reading each and everyone of his novel and never been disapointed. He was a great storyteller captivating readers from begining to end. The author mixes well between the story of a nation and the individual story of the main character. <br/><br/>In this 3rd book, the main character Minke, now an educated young adult, returns to his native count</span>
  <span id="freeText17569860625311644622" style="display:none">This is the third book of the Buru Quartet I've read and the 4th novel I've read from the greatest Indonesian author of all time, Pramoedya Ananta Toer. I've loved reading each and everyone of his novel and never been disapointed. He was a great storyteller captivating readers from begining to end. The author mixes well between the story of a nation and the individual story of the main character. <br /><br />In this 3rd book, the main character Minke, now an educated young adult, returns to his native country after spending years studying and writing short stories in Europe. At the beginning of the 20th century, he returns to the not yet unified Indonesia and still occupied by Netherland. First, while he's confident in his future embracing modernism and the new century, he hesitates in what he wants to do in his personnal and professional life. Then, after firt few experience with mild results, he throws himself into journalism and creating associations to empower indiginous people against the occupying powers. <br /><br />The quartet main theme is struggle against colonialism throught different perspectives. The first 2 books were a coming of age of a young teenage educated in a traditional family discovering life outside protection of family, the real life, and his country. In this book, Minke is a confirmed man who tries to bring his fellow citizens to grow up from tradional education to a well organized and educated country like several other Asian countries had done prior to them. In this book, readers discover Indonesia before the country was unified, while still under occupation, and trying to bring itself together and up into the new century so not to be left behind.<br /><br />This book is a must read book like any book of Pramoedya Ananta Toer. I can't wait to buy and read the 4th book of the buru Quartet.</span>
  <a data-text-id="17569860625311644622" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

    <div class="section">
      

<div id="review_2464682115" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2464682115" />
    <a title="Lisa" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/1758411-lisa"><img alt="Lisa" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1229828252p2/1758411.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2464682115?book_show_action=true">Sep 01, 2019</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Lisa" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Lisa" href="/user/show/1758411-lisa">Lisa</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback 9780140256345" href="/book/show/25306224-footsteps">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1758411-lisa?shelf=translation">translation</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1758411-lisa?shelf=c20th">c20th</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1758411-lisa?shelf=historical-fiction">historical-fiction</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1758411-lisa?shelf=indonesia">indonesia</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1758411-lisa?shelf=series">series</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1758411-lisa?shelf=indobookgroup">indobookgroup</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1758411-lisa?shelf=hidden-history">hidden-history</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2464682115" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer13692541567640098937"><em>Footsteps (Jejak Langkah)</em> is the third in the Pramoedya Ananta Toer’s <em>Buru Quartet,</em> the series of four novels tracing Indonesia's 'awakening' that Toer wrote while in prison on the island of Buru. (<a href='https://anzlitlovers.com/2019/03/06/child-of-all-nations-the-buru-quartet-2-by-pramoedya-ananta-toer-translated-by-max-lane/' rel='nofollow noopener'>See my review of Book 2</a> for the background to this, and also for my thoughts about the translation and introduction which apply equally to this volume). <em>Footsteps </em>is a more 'political' novel, and belongs in that distinctive category of <a href='https://johannesburgreviewofbooks.com/2018/05/07/historical-fiction-is-back-with-a-fire-in-its-belly-fred-khumalo-reflects-on-how-writing-can-be-a-powerful-tool-for-an-activist/' rel='nofollow noopener'>historical fiction as activism</a>, that is, it's written by authors r</span>
  <span id="freeText13692541567640098937" style="display:none"><em>Footsteps (Jejak Langkah)</em> is the third in the Pramoedya Ananta Toer’s <em>Buru Quartet,</em> the series of four novels tracing Indonesia's 'awakening' that Toer wrote while in prison on the island of Buru. (<a href="https://anzlitlovers.com/2019/03/06/child-of-all-nations-the-buru-quartet-2-by-pramoedya-ananta-toer-translated-by-max-lane/" rel="nofollow noopener">See my review of Book 2</a> for the background to this, and also for my thoughts about the translation and introduction which apply equally to this volume). <em>Footsteps </em>is a more 'political' novel, and belongs in that distinctive category of <a href="https://johannesburgreviewofbooks.com/2018/05/07/historical-fiction-is-back-with-a-fire-in-its-belly-fred-khumalo-reflects-on-how-writing-can-be-a-powerful-tool-for-an-activist/" rel="nofollow noopener">historical fiction as activism</a>, that is, it's written by authors redressing the hidden stories and silences of colonised peoples in well-researched fiction. Toer had spent years researching the life of <a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Tirto_Adhi_Soerjo" rel="nofollow noopener">Tirto Adi Suryo</a>, who was the inspiration for this quartet, but Toer's papers were all destroyed when he was arrested and held without trial for fourteen years.<br /><br />Notwithstanding that setback, Toer created this novel from memory, telling the story of a man honoured in 2006 as a <a title="National Hero of Indonesia" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/National_Hero_of_Indonesia" rel="nofollow noopener">National Hero of Indonesia.</a> Toer's central character Minke appears to be a reasonably authentic recreation of Tirto's life, (though the Wikipedia entry in English includes nothing about his personal life, which in the quartet so far, includes three wives.) As Max Lane explains in the Introduction, Tirto was editor of the first Native-owned newspaper and co-founder of the first magazine for women; he initiated a legal advisory service; he co-founded a modern political organisation devoted to developing what would become Indonesian nationalism; and he was a pioneer of indigenous literature in a <em>language of the nation yet to be born. </em><br /><br />NB: My use of terms to describe different ethnic groups and social divisions are those that are used in the book. 'Indonesians' would be anachronistic in the era of the Dutch East Indies, and Toer uses terms like Native, Indo, Indisch, and regional descriptors such as Javanese, Moluccan and Balinese to indicate racial differences while also indicating social differences with terms of address in different languages, like <em>Mas, Gusti Kanjeng, Haji, Sinyo, Meneer, Mevrouw, Ndoro, Teukoe </em>and <em>Princess. </em><br /><br />Books 1 &amp; 2 — <em>This Earth of Mankind</em> (<a href="http://anzlitlovers.com/2018/10/25/this-earth-of-mankind-the-buru-quartet-1-by-pramoedya-ananta-toer-translated-by-max-lane/" rel="nofollow noopener">see here</a>) and <em>Child of All Nations </em>(<a href="http://anzlitlovers.com/2019/03/06/child-of-all-nations-the-buru-quartet-2-by-pramoedya-ananta-toer-translated-by-max-lane/" rel="nofollow noopener">see here</a>) trace the influences on Minke, born into the aristocatic <em>priyani </em>caste and expected to surrender to work as a salaried administrator like his father. But these characters show him a different path to take:<br /> <br /> 	 Annalies, his first Indo (Eurasian) wife, who died after 'repatriation to the Netherlands, because her citizenship was reverted there in order to prevent her inheriting Javanese assets from her Dutch father; <br /> 	 Nyai Ontosoroh, Annalies' mother and concubine to a failed Dutch businessman, whose self-taught efforts rescued the business and whose courage and understanding of the modern colonial world alerted Minke to much injustice; (See <a href="https://anzlitlovers.com/2011/03/17/the-girl-from-the-coast-by-pramoedya-ananta-toer-translated-by-willem-samuels/" rel="nofollow noopener"><em>The Girl from the Coast </em>for Toer's representation of what concubinage was like);</a> <br /> 	 Jean Marais, a French veteran of the war in Aceh who taught Minke to connect with his own people rather than the Dutch at his elite school; <br /> 	 Khouw Ah Soe, an activist for the progress of Chinese people in Java, who was killed by assassins from a Chinese secret society; <br /> 	 Thoenodongso, a peasant who led an uprising against the colonial sugar barons; <br /> 	 Magda Peters, his Dutch teacher at the elite HBS school, who recognised Minke as a future leader (and got herself sent back to Holland because of it); and <br /> 	 Herbert de la Croix, a liberal Dutch administrator and his two daughters, who return to Holland in disillusionment. <br /> <br />So, <em>Footsteps </em>starts in 1901 with Minke at the medical school for Natives. This school was a belated initiative by the Dutch in the wake of international embarrassment about their colonial regime, but its graduates are condemned to serve only as badly-paid doctors attempting to lift the life expectancy of Natives from a shocking 40 years. Minke makes few friends, but is visited by Ter Haar, a liberal Dutch journalist who improves his status at the school by engineering invitations to the Harmoni Club, where he meets Van Kollewijn, a liberal MP espousing <a href="https://www.britannica.com/event/Ethical-Policy" rel="nofollow noopener">the Ethical Policy aimed at improving the welfare of the Natives</a>; <a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/J._B._van_Heutsz" rel="nofollow noopener">General van Heutsz</a>, the man who led the slaughter against the Acehnese; and <a href="https://nl.wikipedia.org/wiki/Marie_van_Zeggelen" rel="nofollow noopener">Marie Van Zeggelen</a>, an author who wrote books supportive of Native freedom including a biography of <a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Kartini" rel="nofollow noopener">Kartini</a>, (a pioneer of girls' education who is referenced in <em>Footsteps</em> as 'the girl from Jepara). These contacts with powerful people enable Minke to flout school rules with impunity, but he ends up abandoning his course to take up journalism.<br /><br /><em>Footsteps </em>isn't a book that flows smoothly; Toer was at pains to make various political points, and so there are jerky sequences of events and occasionally awkward conversations that are included as activism rather than as part of a credible plot. His Native characters are generally more convincing than the stereotypes he uses to convey opinions held by colonials or ethnic identities not from the Indies. Two topics discussed in an unlikely conversation between a <em>very</em> young Minke and these powerful people are raised at the ironically-named Harmoni club:<br /> <br /> 	 Van Kollewjin talks about Holland owing a moral and financial debt to the Indies because exports under the Culture (Forced Cultivation) System saved Holland from bankruptcy, paid for Holland's infrastructure development and provided it with capital for expansion. <br /> 	 Marie Van Zeggelen tackles General Van Heutsz over his use of the word 'unify' instead of 'expand' to describe the conquest of Aceh. He talks of 'pockets' of 'political enclaves' 'destabilising the Indies' and how they must be brought to 'acknowledge the sovereignty of Her Majesty'. Ter Haar and Van Zeggelen argue that they are independent states, and that the aim of these operations is conquest not unification. They ask what his plans are for East Papua and Southeast Papua, while sarcastically noting that <em>West Papua is a heavy burden for the Indies</em>. <br /> <br />Questions of (and activism in support of) recompense for Holland's moral and financial debt, and the territorial integrity of Papua and Aceh under Indonesian sovereignty remain pertinent today.<br /><br />To read the rest of my review please visit <a target="_blank" rel="noopener nofollow" href="https://anzlitlovers.com/2019/09/01/footsteps-the-buru-quartet-3-by-pramoedya-ananta-toer-translated-by-max-lane/">https://anzlitlovers.com/2019/09/01/f...</a></span>
  <a data-text-id="13692541567640098937" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<span id="freeTextContainer15159387168446444391">Footsteps by Pramoedya Ananta Toer<br/><br/>Third book in the Buru Quartet. Minke who we have followed from a teenager in “This Earth of Mankind” and “Child of All Nations” grows to become a man and a political being in this book. This book synthesizes the plot structure and the politics of the first two books and adds on a great historical emphasis to bring these two aspects closely together. Though dense at times, because of historical reference, it is not an unbearable weight, but more so a corridor wi</span>
  <span id="freeText15159387168446444391" style="display:none">Footsteps by Pramoedya Ananta Toer<br /><br />Third book in the Buru Quartet. Minke who we have followed from a teenager in “This Earth of Mankind” and “Child of All Nations” grows to become a man and a political being in this book. This book synthesizes the plot structure and the politics of the first two books and adds on a great historical emphasis to bring these two aspects closely together. Though dense at times, because of historical reference, it is not an unbearable weight, but more so a corridor with many doors asking to be opened and explored more, especially for those like me that do not have a good background in Indonesian history. Central themes of the book on the political level are; rebellion through modern organization, the role of media to unite and legally fight oppression, and the conflict of ethical structures between generations due to “modernization.” <br /><br />I can’t wait to start the last book in the series; “House of Glass.”<br /><br />Some quick favorite quotes:<br /><br />Minke describing his role in the modern organization of the Sakerat Dagang Islamiyah, which he is using to “advance” his people, which is to save his people from being “free slaves,” but to do this he must sacrifice part of their heritage:<br />“In any case our business is not the past but the present. The modern present. A time where people calculate what is useful and what is not, and discard what is not useful…And his, and mine, a people who have been conquered now for centuries, as a people who have lost land and sea as well as ourselves. All that is left is our history, which we still carry. And now I come along and want to steal that too” (377).<br /><br />Critique of modernism:<br />“In the modern world, everything is specialization. People will become alienated from each other. People will have cause to meet only because of business or they will meet by accident. You will no longer be able to tell if the person you are treating is a good man or not”(129).<br /><br /><br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="15159387168446444391" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

<span id="freeTextContainer9284000628310724163">The third book in the Buru quartet continues the story of Minke and his quest to gain power, independence and freedom for he and other Indonesian Natives. This book moves away from the first two in that all of the other characters beside Minke are minor. But new characters are introduced. Minke also moves to a new city, a large city and begins to establish a movement to bring greater power and freedom to his own people.<br/><br/>At its heart this book is a story about a journey. It is a journey of a boy t</span>
  <span id="freeText9284000628310724163" style="display:none">The third book in the Buru quartet continues the story of Minke and his quest to gain power, independence and freedom for he and other Indonesian Natives. This book moves away from the first two in that all of the other characters beside Minke are minor. But new characters are introduced. Minke also moves to a new city, a large city and begins to establish a movement to bring greater power and freedom to his own people.<br /><br />At its heart this book is a story about a journey. It is a journey of a boy turning into a young man and this young man turning into a man. All the while his country is also going on a journey with him as one of its surprising leaders.<br /><br />I have loved this story. I have loved the progress, the setbacks, the turmoil, the friendship and the hatred felt within it. It continued to show the immorality of colonialism and the despicableness of racism. Above all else it showed the beginnings of human rights for all people regardless of sex, age, race, religion, marital status, occupation, creed or abilities. This is something we are still struggling with today. Minke is an inspiration that helps me want to continue the fight and help those who can't help themselves.</span>

  <div class="left bodycol">

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Chris Wharton" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Chris Wharton" href="/user/show/18899975-chris-wharton">Chris Wharton</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="ebook 9781101615348" href="/book/show/333078.Footsteps">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/18899975-chris-wharton?shelf=1-condo-read">1-condo-read</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/18899975-chris-wharton?shelf=explore-colony-empire">explore-colony-empire</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/18899975-chris-wharton?shelf=malay-indo-spore">malay-indo-spore</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/18899975-chris-wharton?shelf=women">women</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/18899975-chris-wharton?shelf=seasia">seasia</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/18899975-chris-wharton?shelf=classic-writer-or-work-from-past">classic-writer-or-work-from-past</a>,

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2883743514" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer12970849886821501385">The third, and longest, of the Buru Quartet on rising Indonesian nationalism in the early years of the 20th century. Minke, the protagonist, drops out of medical school (although he was the first native to be admitted) in Batavia (now Jakarta) and returns to political organizing. Apart from the suspicion and opposition of the Dutch colonial administration, the mixed-race populations, and traditional native upper classes, some of whom thrived under the Dutch even while being coopted, he faces the</span>
  <span id="freeText12970849886821501385" style="display:none">The third, and longest, of the Buru Quartet on rising Indonesian nationalism in the early years of the 20th century. Minke, the protagonist, drops out of medical school (although he was the first native to be admitted) in Batavia (now Jakarta) and returns to political organizing. Apart from the suspicion and opposition of the Dutch colonial administration, the mixed-race populations, and traditional native upper classes, some of whom thrived under the Dutch even while being coopted, he faces the additional challenge of uniting multiple traditional kingdoms comprising myriad ethnicities, including immigrant Chinese, and language and religious groups, many of them poor and illiterate, in one nationalist movement across the region’s expansive stretches of island archipelagoes. Means of organizing, the pros and cons of various political strategies, the language(s) to be used, educational strategies, publications to spread the word, etc, are all parts of this challenge. Some of this is a bit dry and pedantic, but it is also informative and interesting about the difficulties faced in the particular historical circumstances. Within these cicrumstances (perhaps the most fascinating aspect of the book), the plot moves on many fronts with a variety of characters through moments of tension, defeats and setbacks, and victories and incremental progress. At the same time, Minke continues to confront personal ordeals in marriage, friendships, rivalries both friendly and unfriendly, physical attacks and threats on his life, and, finally, arrest.</span>
  <a data-text-id="12970849886821501385" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

    <a title="Ratih Latifah" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/88840292-ratih-latifah"><img alt="Ratih Latifah" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1601481722p2/88840292.jpg" /></a>

    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">

        <a title="Ratih Latifah" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Ratih Latifah" href="/user/show/88840292-ratih-latifah">Ratih Latifah</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2582022124" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer15930754603291073867">I've read the first and second book in early 2018 and this third book from Buru quartet has been postponed due to changing book-list priority (to be read-list) and also the messed up of my 5th semester :')<br/><br/>Crying and crying over each plot when it's describing Minke's love story. Princess Van Kasiruta who is a daughter of King Kasiruta, An Sang Mei who is a Chinese English teacher, their life </span>
  <span id="freeText15930754603291073867" style="display:none">I've read the first and second book in early 2018 and this third book from Buru quartet has been postponed due to changing book-list priority (to be read-list) and also the messed up of my 5th semester :')<br /><br />Crying and crying over each plot when it's describing Minke's love story. I'm so overwhelmed about the woman character in this book. So amazed be how strong and charming they are. Princess Van Kasiruta who is a daughter of King Kasiruta, An Sang Mei who is a Chinese English teacher, their life was so much complicated !!<br />This book was made me dumbfounded, highly amazed by the struggles minke has been thru for growing up nationalism in indigenes' mind. Minke has tried every way until Medan daily newspaper and Sarikat Dagang Islam succeeded.<br />Near the end of this book was the climax. When Minke was under arrest and he wrote a farewell letter and a divorce letter all at once. (Bcs he has to go far away from Java and probably will never come back).<br /><br />"Berbahagialah dia yang tak tahu sesuatu. Pengetahuan, perbandingan, membuat orang tahu tempatnya sendiri, dan tempat orang lain, gelisah dalam alam perbandingan." (pg. 203)<br /><br />I made a poem for this book in bahasa :<br />Apalah aku,<br />di antara perempuan-perempuan<br />yang tak goyah<br />tak kalah<br />di hadapan keangkuhan sejarah"<br />-rlm</span>

<div id="review_3568890931" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/3568890931" />
    <a title="Andrada" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/4864790-andrada"><img alt="Andrada" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1494861282p2/4864790.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/3568890931?book_show_action=true">Oct 24, 2020</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Andrada" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Andrada" href="/user/show/4864790-andrada">Andrada</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="ebook 9781101615348" href="/book/show/333078.Footsteps">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4864790-andrada?shelf=modern-classics">modern-classics</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer3568890931" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer5824046557338795456">The ideological groundwork set up by Pramoedya in Child of all Nations comes to fruition in Footsteps as Minke reaches maturity and struggles to find the right path to best nurture the burgeoning nationalism of the Dutch East Indies. <br/><br/>While big debates weighed down the second book of the Buru Quartet, Footsteps delves too much into the political, detailing the rise, fall and woes of different organizations set up by the Natives for their advancement and the protection of their interests in the fa</span>
  <span id="freeText5824046557338795456" style="display:none">The ideological groundwork set up by Pramoedya in Child of all Nations comes to fruition in Footsteps as Minke reaches maturity and struggles to find the right path to best nurture the burgeoning nationalism of the Dutch East Indies. <br /><br />While big debates weighed down the second book of the Buru Quartet, Footsteps delves too much into the political, detailing the rise, fall and woes of different organizations set up by the Natives for their advancement and the protection of their interests in the face of colonial authorities. And while it was interesting to see how these organizations were created and thrived, at times the way Pramoedya presents them is close to a dry historical account. I also felt like the moment they entered the story, everything else became secondary. I much preferred the first part of the novel, that was centered on Minke and his struggles as a medical student than the detailed account of the various organizations in the second half. <br /><br />I also didn’t like the fact that, although some characters from the previous two books showed up, nothing is said about what has happened to them and they become two-dimensional. I’m thinking here in particular of Robert Suurhoff and Panji Darman. <br /><br />After the ending of Footsteps, I have a bad feeling about how the quartet is going to end, but I suppose it was inevitable!</span>
  <a data-text-id="5824046557338795456" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

    <a title="Edwina Shaddick" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/39299820-edwina-shaddick"><img alt="Edwina Shaddick" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1421591001p2/39299820.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2717349649?book_show_action=true">Feb 20, 2019</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Edwina Shaddick" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Edwina Shaddick" href="/user/show/39299820-edwina-shaddick">Edwina Shaddick</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

          <a class="lightGreyText" title="ebook 9781101615348" href="/book/show/333078.Footsteps">review of another edition</a>


        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
                  <em>
                    This review has been hidden because it contains spoilers. To view it,
                    <a href="#" onclick="Effect.toggle(&#39;reviewTextContainer2717349649&#39;); return false;">click here.</a>
                  </em>
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2717349649" class="readable"
                    style="display:none"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer9084831258352647015">Absolutely incredible. I preferred this to Rizal's Noli and while I think it's as good as Tagore's Home and the World, I'm fonder of this one.<br/><br/>It was fascinating to see the protagonist Minke stumble into activism, and I appreciated the inclusion of his mistakes. He is urged by many people to organise but he doesn't know how. He starts an organisation but later realises he's designed it in a way that will make it unpopular with regular folk, and it dies an early death. We also see him trying to re</span>
  <span id="freeText9084831258352647015" style="display:none">Absolutely incredible. I preferred this to Rizal's Noli and while I think it's as good as Tagore's Home and the World, I'm fonder of this one.<br /><br />It was fascinating to see the protagonist Minke stumble into activism, and I appreciated the inclusion of his mistakes. He is urged by many people to organise but he doesn't know how. He starts an organisation but later realises he's designed it in a way that will make it unpopular with regular folk, and it dies an early death. We also see him trying to reconcile his desire for a multiracial decolonial movement with the undeserved advantages that the Chinese, Arabs and Indos (eurasians) enjoy. He rails against the superstitions and hierarchy of Javanese culture, but feels conflicted about betraying his mother's culture. I liked how we got to see his activism informed by the goings-on in China, South Africa, and the Philippines.</span>
  <a data-text-id="9084831258352647015" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

<div id="review_3336378202" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/3336378202" />
    <a title="Xing Yi Ngiam" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/91432551-xing-yi-ngiam"><img alt="Xing Yi Ngiam" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1546357602p2/91432551.jpg" /></a>

              <span id="reviewTextContainer3336378202" class="readable"

<span id="freeTextContainer4456597092694183573">Four stars because it is not an easy read, especially for readers who have never read the first two installments of the Buru Quartet and lacking knowledge of some historical details. As with any other translation, the loss of the original beauty of the language also hinders full appreciation of the text. <br/><br/>But I never tire of reminding friends that Pramoedya wrote this in prison, from memory, without reference material, with writing materials covertly obtained. This work remains a gigantic literar</span>
  <span id="freeText4456597092694183573" style="display:none">Four stars because it is not an easy read, especially for readers who have never read the first two installments of the Buru Quartet and lacking knowledge of some historical details. As with any other translation, the loss of the original beauty of the language also hinders full appreciation of the text. <br /><br />But I never tire of reminding friends that Pramoedya wrote this in prison, from memory, without reference material, with writing materials covertly obtained. This work remains a gigantic literary and historical masterpiece. It stirred a deep emotional response in me, and surpasses most other superficial anti-colonial writing that I have read.</span>

              <span id="reviewTextContainer3472692966" class="readable"

<span id="freeTextContainer12658298751336770525">Longer and more political than the other books in the Buru Quartet, this third one sometimes grows so political and dry in its positioning of the emergence of Indonesia as a nation of its own that I almost miss some of the more soap opera moments of the first two novels. Minke (the narrator) is maturing, but still not always wise, and no matter what success he has in bringing forth that national consciousness, he remains constantly thwarted by largely European interests still dedicated to practi</span>
  <span id="freeText12658298751336770525" style="display:none">Longer and more political than the other books in the Buru Quartet, this third one sometimes grows so political and dry in its positioning of the emergence of Indonesia as a nation of its own that I almost miss some of the more soap opera moments of the first two novels. Minke (the narrator) is maturing, but still not always wise, and no matter what success he has in bringing forth that national consciousness, he remains constantly thwarted by largely European interests still dedicated to practicing all the usual exploitative strategies of colonialism. The Quartet at large is a very important book, but not at all easy to read, nor sometimes like.</span>
  <a data-text-id="12658298751336770525" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

<span id="freeTextContainer5229906589538094049">This book is a bit tough compare to the other 2 earlier books ( this earth of mankind and child of all nations). I can understand this book supposed to be dry, this is the era just before indonesia's independence.   <span id="freeText5229906589538094049" style="display:none">This book is a bit tough compare to the other 2 earlier books ( this earth of mankind and child of all nations). I can understand this book supposed to be dry, this is the era just before indonesia's independence. There are so many names listed as this was the time when they started building up the native associations which later on involved a lot in politic. There are so many political movement told here, the ones in indonesia like bali and sumatera. Many local heroic names were mentioned as well. Pramodya covered the war across the world as well during this time, especially philipines and japan. I am glad i finally completed this book. I know i have to come back to read this book again with the fresh look to understand better what is happening with all these youth social and political movement that eventually triggered indonesia independence. <br /><br />If you read this series, you will understand Pramoedya did a nice chronological order of indonesia's history before the independence and right after that. The first book described how the native indonesians had to adjust culturally and adapt the influence from the dutch. The second book speak so much about the liberal movement in europe mostly that influence some of the dutch to think differently about colonialism. This spark the opportunity to flourish the native political and social movement. We also learn other tribes that come to indonesia along with the dutch at that time like thr trader from arab and china. We also have a bit of jest of chinese political movement that spread all the way to indonesia. <br /><br />Minke as the main character had grown along the story. He is a consistent rebel since the beginning of the book. The brightest one, the most educated one and the idealist one. As i said we can easily fall in love with minke.<br /><br />Pramoedya is rich with information, this is not just a story but a history landmark too.</span>

<div id="review_2389731779" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2389731779" />
    <a title="Carol Chapin" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/41252532-carol-chapin"><img alt="Carol Chapin" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1426465457p2/41252532.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2389731779?book_show_action=true">Sep 10, 2018</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Carol Chapin" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Carol Chapin" href="/user/show/41252532-carol-chapin">Carol Chapin</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="ebook 9781101615348" href="/book/show/333078.Footsteps">review of another edition</a>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2389731779" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer11840029967739554460">This is the third book of four that tells the story of Minke, a native of Java under Dutch rule, at the beginning of the twentieth century. These books become better as they go, and this one was outstanding. This book begins with Minke’s entry into medical school in Betawi (now Jakarta). The political awareness that began in the last part of his life continues and increases rapidly. The book covers a number of years in Minke’s life. He attends medical school for five years, but drops out before </span>
  <span id="freeText11840029967739554460" style="display:none">This is the third book of four that tells the story of Minke, a native of Java under Dutch rule, at the beginning of the twentieth century. These books become better as they go, and this one was outstanding. This book begins with Minke’s entry into medical school in Betawi (now Jakarta). The political awareness that began in the last part of his life continues and increases rapidly. The book covers a number of years in Minke’s life. He attends medical school for five years, but drops out before graduating and starts the first Native magazine in the Indies – which later became a daily newspaper. He starts several societies, organizations to advance the cause of the peoples of the Indies against Dutch control. This is a complex, intellectual novel. It describes the multitude of difficulties in organizing against a colonial power. One begins to realize the extreme diversity of the Dutch East Indies. Dutch governor-generals sent one ethnic group to conquer others. Language was a key to many difficulties. Minke’s organization began in Java, and many members believed that business should be conducted in Javanese. But Minke supported Malay as a language more suiting to reaching more people (and common Malay, not “school” or “government” Malay). Dutch served as a common tongue as well. The social structures of each ethnic group were complex, and the various titles and honorifics were hard to follow - but important in how they were used. All this was very interesting. <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[ As Minke progresses in publishing and organizing, dealing with all the various factions and opinions, he emerges as a leader of the opposition. While initially only being carefully watched by the Dutch powers, at the end of this novel he is arrested on trumped up charges. <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span></span>
  <a data-text-id="11840029967739554460" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

He got them involved through organizing a party (though atually it was not political and more on strenghtening the Indonesian's economic life) and a mass me</span>
  <span id="freeText9983572587192280982" style="display:none">This is the third book from Pram's tetralogy. This book is wonderful in how historical details could be provided and clear description of the events showed. In this book, the main character of the book, Minke, started his move to against the colonial. He moved the Indonesian people through moving Indonesian people to be involved in politics. He got them involved through organizing a party (though atually it was not political and more on strenghtening the Indonesian's economic life) and a mass media (in which many of his articles and writings badly attacked the colonial government that they got outraged at him). Unfortunately, his sincere attempts to fight for Indonesia was not followed by the other Indonesians. In fact, Minke's efforts were crumbled by some corrupt Indonesian. However, this book shows me how a man should stand for his nation despite all the difficulties and challenges.A good book you must absolutely read!The historical details can be a lil bit boring but it is very enjoyable!</span>
  <a data-text-id="9983572587192280982" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  <span id="freeText9119190825117597985" style="display:none"><a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[<br />I didn't like this book as much as This Earth of Mankind and Child of All Nation. <br />This is a book where the beginning and ending are shocking, but the middle part absolutely boring. Maybe it's because I find economic and political matters difficult to understand. But I also didn't like Minke anymore, even Nyai for moving out of the country and her new relationship. In short, I didn't like the old characther anymore. I haven't acquainted myself enough to really know the new characters, but I found the new ones interesting and refreshing. <br />Also I just realized in this book that Minke doesn't like Indos. I hate Minke for "forgetting" Annelies, I know she's dead and it's a painful memory. But Minke always praises Mei, who is also his dead wife. I guess I miss Annelies.<br /><br />This is the last book written from Minke's perspective. I hope 4th book will not be disappointing. <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span></span>

  function submitShelfLink(unique_id, book_id, shelf_id, shelf_name, submit_form, exclusive) {
    var checkbox_id = 'shelf_name_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    var element = document.getElementById(checkbox_id)

    var checked = element.checked
    if (checked && exclusive) {
      // can't uncheck a radio by clicking it!
      return
    }
    if(document.getElementById("savingMessage")){
      Element.show('savingMessage')
    }
    var element_id = 'shelfInDropdownName_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    Element.update(element_id, "saving...");
    if (submit_form) {
      Element.hide('shelfDropdown_' + unique_id)
      var form = document.getElementById('addBookForm' + book_id)
      if (form) {
        form.shelf.value = shelf_name
        form.onsubmit()
      }
    }
    else {
      var action = checked ? 'remove' : ''
      element.checked = !element.checked

    }
  }

    afterShelfSave(checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name.escapeHTML())
  }

Pada saat yang sama, Dimas menerima k<\/span>\n  <span id=\"freeText11999708404257278312\" style=\"display:none\">Paris, Mei 1968. \n\nKetika revolusi mahasiswa berkecamuk di Paris, Dimas Suryo seorang eksil politik Indonesia bertemu Vivienne Deveraux, seorang mahasiswa Prancis yang ikut demonstrasi melawan pemerintah Prancis. Pada saat yang sama, Dimas menerima kabar dari Jakarta: Hananto Prawiro, sahabatnya, ditangkap tentara dan dinyatakan tewas. Dimas merasa cemas dan gamang. Bersama puluhan wartawan dan seniman lain, dia tak bisa kembali ke Jakarta karena paspornya dicabut oleh pemerintah Indonesia. Sejak itu mereka mengelana tanpa status yang jelas dari Santiago ke Havana, ke Peking dan akhirnya mendarat di tanah Eropa untuk mendapatkan suaka dan menetap di sana.\n\nDi tengah kesibukan mengelola Restoran Tanah Air di Paris bersama tiga kawannya: Nug, Tjai, dan Risjaf—mereka berempat disebut Empat Pilar Tanah Air—Dimas, terus-menerus dikejar rasa bersalah karena kawan-kawannya di Indonesia satu persatu tumbang, dikejar, ditembak, atau menghilang begitu saja dalam perburuan Peristiwa 30 September. Max is an inspirational figure, but he is also a flawed idealist wh<\/span>\n  <span id=\"freeText18232652613691390742\" style=\"display:none\">Max Havelaar - a Dutch civil servant in Java - burns with an insatiable desire to end the ill treatment and oppression inflicted on the native peoples by the colonial administration. Max is an inspirational figure, but he is also a flawed idealist whose vow to protect the Javanese from cruelty ends in his own downfall. In Max Havelaar, Multatuli (the pseudonym for Eduard Douwes Dekker) vividly recreated his own experiences in Java and tellingly depicts the hypocrisy of those who gained from the corrupt coffee trade. Sending shockwaves through the Dutch nation when it was published in 1860, this damning exposé of the terrible conditions in the colonies led to welfare reforms in Java and continues to inspire the fairtrade movement today.\n\nRoy Edwards\'s vibrant translation conveys the satirical and innovative style of Multatuli\'s autobiographical polemic. In his introduction, R. P. <div class='bookAuthorProfile__about'>

<span id="freeTextContainer6852951342127533845">Pramoedya Ananta Toer was an Indonesian author of novels, short stories, essays, polemics, and histories of his homeland and its people. A well-regarded writer in the West, Pramoedya's outspoken and often politically charged writings faced censorship in his native land during the pre-reformation era. For opposing the policies of both founding president Sukarno, as well as those of its successor, t</span>
  <span id="freeText6852951342127533845" style="display:none">Pramoedya Ananta Toer was an Indonesian author of novels, short stories, essays, polemics, and histories of his homeland and its people. A well-regarded writer in the West, Pramoedya's outspoken and often politically charged writings faced censorship in his native land during the pre-reformation era. For opposing the policies of both founding president Sukarno, as well as those of its successor, the New Order regime of Suharto, he faced extrajudicial punishment. During the many years in which he suffered imprisonment and house arrest, he became a cause célèbre for advocates of freedom of expression and human rights.<br /><br />Bibliography:<br />* Kranji-Bekasi Jatuh (1947)<br />* Perburuan (The Fugitive) (1950)<br />* Keluarga Gerilya (1950)<br />* Bukan Pasarmalam (1951)<br />* Cerita dari Blora (1952)<br />* Gulat di Jakarta (1953)<br />* Korupsi (Corruption) (1954)<br />* Midah - Si Manis Bergigi Emas (1954)<br />* Cerita Calon Arang (The King, the Witch, and the Priest) (1957)<br />* Hoakiau di Indonesia (1960)<br />* Panggil Aku Kartini Saja I &amp; II (1962)<br />* The Buru Quartet<br /> o Bumi Manusia (This Earth of Mankind) (1980)<br /> o Anak Semua Bangsa (Child of All Nations) (1980)<br /> o Jejak Langkah (Footsteps) (1985)<br /> o Rumah Kaca (House of Glass) (1988)<br />* Gadis Pantai (The Girl from the Coast) (1982)<br />* Nyanyi Sunyi Seorang Bisu (A Mute's Soliloquy) (1995)<br />* Arus Balik (1995)<br />* Arok Dedes (1999)<br />* Mangir (1999)<br />* Larasati (2000)<br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="6852951342127533845" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

</div>

A novel of heroism, passion, and betrayal, it provides a spectacular conclusion to a series hailed as one of the great works of modern literature. At the start of House of Glass, Minke, writer and leader of the dissident movement, is now imprisoned--and the narrative has switched to Pangemanann, a former policeman, who has the task of spying and reporting on those who continue the struggle for independence. But the hunter is becoming the hunted. Pangemanann is a victim of his own conscience and has come to admire his adversaries. He must decide whether the law is to safeguard the rights of the people or to control the people. He fears the loss of his position, his family, and his self-respect. This partial loads on almost every page view.  The associated React component makes
a call to SignInPromptController#get to determine if the user should see the sign in interstial.
This is determined by how many signed out pagehits the user has executed an how recently they have
last seen the insterstitial.  If the controller responds indicating the popup should appear, the
